# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: rust_blockchain_nft_expert_071_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: rust
**Context Length**: 873424 tokens
**Files**: 83

## Task Title

Architectural Blueprint for Fractional NFT (F-NFT) Integration

## Description

The CanvasChain Symphony platform is looking to introduce a major new feature: Fractional NFTs (F-NFTs). This will allow a single, high-value NFT to be 'sharded' into multiple, fungible tokens that can be owned and traded by different users. This feature aims to increase liquidity and make high-value assets more accessible. This task requires creating a comprehensive architectural plan for integrating F-NFTs into the existing microservices-based system, without writing the implementation code. The focus is on impact analysis, component design, and data flow across the entire architecture.

## Your Task

You are the lead architect for the CanvasChain Symphony project. Your task is to produce a detailed technical design document for the upcoming Fractional NFT (F-NFT) feature. Your document should be a roadmap for the development team.

Your analysis must include:
1.  **Impact Analysis**: Identify every service, shared crate, and critical file that will be impacted by the introduction of F-NFTs.
2.  **Data Model Changes**: Propose specific changes to the core data structures, particularly within the `ccs_common` crate, to represent fractional ownership.
3.  **Component-Level Design**: For each impacted microservice (`node_service`, `minting_service`, `wallet_service`, `marketplace_service`, etc.), detail the necessary changes. This includes:
    - New or modified gRPC/RPC endpoints.
    - Changes to business logic modules (e.g., `staking_logic.rs`, `auction_engine.rs`).
    - Modifications to state management (`state_machine.rs`, `state_db.rs`).
4.  **Core User Flows**: Describe the end-to-end sequence of operations and inter-service communication for two key user flows:
    a.  An owner fractionalizing their existing NFT.
    b.  A new user purchasing a fraction of an NFT on the marketplace.
5.  **API & Configuration**: Detail the required changes to the `api_gateway` (including the OpenAPI spec) and any new configuration parameters needed in the `.toml` configuration files.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task systematically:

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance**: Review high-level documentation like `docs/architecture.md`, `docs/adr/001-monorepo-for-microservices.md`, and `docs/adr/002-grpc-and-event-bus.md` to confirm the overall system design (microservices, monorepo, gRPC communication).
2.  **Identify the Core Abstraction**: Recognize that the concept of an 'NFT' is central. The first step is to locate its definition, likely in `crates/ccs_common/src/nft.rs`. The plan would start by proposing changes here, such as adding a new struct `FractionalInfo` to the main `Nft` struct, or creating a new top-level `F-NFT` enum variant.
3.  **Trace the State Transition**: Understand that any change to ownership or state must be validated by the core blockchain logic. The developer would immediately investigate `services/node_service/src/state_machine.rs` to determine how new transaction types are handled. A new transaction type, e.g., `Transaction::Fractionalize`, would be proposed.
4.  **Service-by-Service Impact Analysis**: The developer would then methodically go through each service's directory:
    - **`minting_service`**: Propose a new gRPC endpoint for the fractionalization process. This would involve changes in `logic/nft_factory.rs` to handle the creation of fractional tokens linked to a parent NFT.
    - **`wallet_service`**: Propose updates to the wallet's data structures and RPC server to query and display fractional ownership, not just whole NFTs. This touches `key_manager.rs` and `rpc_server.rs`.
    - **`marketplace_service`**: Propose significant changes to `listing_manager.rs` and `auction_engine.rs` to allow listings, bids, and sales of fractions. This implies pricing per-fraction.
    - **`governance_service`**: Consider the implications. If voting is based on NFT holdings, how do fractions count? This requires analyzing `proposal_engine.rs`.
    - **`api_gateway`**: Map out the new public-facing REST endpoints in `rest_api.rs` and update the gRPC client calls in `grpc_client.rs` to communicate with the backend services. The `docs/api/gateway_openapi.yaml` would need corresponding updates.
5.  **Shared Crates**: Identify necessary changes in `ccs_proto` to add new gRPC messages and services, and in `ccs_db` to handle the new state storage requirements in `state_db.rs`.
6.  **Synthesize Flows**: Document the end-to-end flows by creating sequence diagrams or detailed textual descriptions showing the chain of gRPC calls from the `api_gateway` to the relevant backend services, culminating in a transaction processed by the `node_service`.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Completeness of Impact Analysis**: Did the agent correctly identify the majority of impacted services (node, minting, wallet, marketplace, api_gateway, governance) and shared crates (ccs_common, ccs_proto, ccs_db)?
- **Correctness of Proposed Changes**: Are the proposed changes consistent with the existing architecture (e.g., using gRPC, modifying the state machine for core logic)?
- **Depth of Component-Level Detail**: Does the analysis go beyond surface-level statements? Does it pinpoint specific files, modules, and functions (e.g., `state_machine.rs`, `auction_engine.rs`) that need modification?
- **Logical Coherence of User Flows**: Are the described end-to-end communication flows for fractionalization and purchasing logical and technically sound within the project's architecture?
- **Identification of Core Abstractions**: Did the agent correctly identify the modification of `ccs_common/src/nft.rs` and the introduction of a new transaction type in `node_service` as the foundational changes?
- **Architectural Reasoning**: Does the agent's plan implicitly or explicitly demonstrate an understanding of why changes must be made in a certain way (e.g., why state changes must be validated by the consensus nodes and not just in a peripheral service)?

    10→## ✨ Why CanvasChain?
    11→
    12→Digital art keeps evolving—so should the chain it lives on. CanvasChain Symphony lets creators compose evolving, multi-layer NFTs that react to collectors, governance votes, DeFi staking and real-world events. Each **movement** of the symphony is a standalone Rust micro-service you can fork, extend or swap out.
    13→
    14→* Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI) consensus blends PoS staking with VRF randomness to pick a “composer node.”
    15→* Factory & Proxy patterns spawn user-defined NFT instruments with upgradeable logic.
    16→* Event-driven gRPC mesh keeps services decoupled yet reactive.
    17→* Strategy pattern supports pluggable crypto curves (Ed25519, BLS12-381, SPHINCS+, …).
    18→* Observer + State Machine render live ownership & trait evolution.

     1→# 001 – Adopt a Monorepo for Rust Microservices
     2→
     3→Status: **Approved**  
     4→Date: 2024-06-17  
     5→Tags: `repository`, `dev‐experience`, `ci/cd`, `rust`, `microservices`
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## Context
    10→
    11→CanvasChain Symphony orchestrates ten specialized Rust microservices—`composition`, `minting`, `remixing`, `marketplace`, `royalty`, `wallet`, `governance`, `token-management`, `defi`, and `orchestrator`.  
    12→Early prototypes lived in independent Git repositories. While this respected bounded context, it created friction:
    13→
    14→* **Version skew**: cross-service protocol buffers, domain types and cryptographic primitives (e.g., our pluggable `CurveStrategy`) drifted, forcing tedious cherry-picks.
    15→* **Atomic evolution**: a change to a shared crate (e.g., `canvas-chain-primitives`) required synchronized releases across repos; partial updates risked network halts.
    16→* **CI💰**: each repo ran its own CI minutes; caching was duplicated and expensive.
    17→* **Dev onboarding**: cloning ten repos, wiring SSH deploy keys and remembering divergent release processes slowed contributors.
    18→
    19→Rust’s native support for [Cargo workspaces](https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch14-03-cargo-workspaces.html) and our need for atomic, protocol-grade versioning make a monorepo attractive.
    20→
    21→## Decision
    22→
    23→We will:
    24→
    25→1. Move all Rust microservices, shared crates (`*-primitives`, `*-proto`, etc.) and infrastructure scripts into a single repository named `canvaschain-symphony`.
    26→2. Organize code using Cargo workspaces:
    27→
    28→```
    29→canvaschain-symphony/
    30→├── Cargo.toml            # root workspace manifest
    31→├── crates/
    32→│   ├── primitive
... (truncated)

     1→# ADR 002: gRPC for Service-to-Service RPC and NATS Event Bus for Asynchronous Messaging
     2→
     3→Date: 2023-11-12  
     4→Status: Accepted  
     5→Supersedes: —  
     6→Superseded by: —  
     7→Authors: Core Architecture Team (CanvasChain Symphony)
     8→
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. Context
    12→
    13→CanvasChain Symphony is composed of ten autonomous Rust micro-services—`composer`, `minter`, `remixer`, `market-maker`, `royalty-streamer`, etc. Each service is owned and deployed independently yet must inter-operate to deliver end-to-end user flows. Two communication patterns are required:
    14→
    15→1. **Request / Response (RPC)**  
    16→   Example: the `market-maker` service must synchronously query `token-registry` for the current royalty split before quoting a swap.
    17→
    18→2. **Publish / Subscribe (Eventing)**  
    19→   Example: the `governance` service votes on a “movement” that triggers the `composer` to mint the next artwork. Every interested service (`gallery-renderer`, `royalty-streamer`, `analytics`) must react to the same chain event without tight coupling.
    20→
    21→Key non-functional drivers:
    22→
    23→* **Performance:** high throughput, low latency, binary payloads (art layers can be large).
    24→* **Language Inter-op:** we anticipate plug-ins in Python (ML models), WASM (browser previews), and potentially Solidity-compiled bindings.
    25→* **Back-Pressure & Delivery Guarantees:** at-least-once delivery for critical NFT state transitions, but fire-and-forget for analytics streams.
    26→* **Security:** end-to-end encryption (mTLS), pluggable authN/authZ compatible with our wallet integration.
    27→
    28→---
    29→
    30→## 2. Decision
    31→
    32→1. **gRPC** will be adopted for all synchronou

     2→# Architecture Decision Record 003  
     3→**Pluggable Cryptography Strategy**
     4→
     5→| Status | Proposed |
     6→| ------ | -------- |
     7→| Date   | 2024-05-05 |
     8→| Target release | `v0.8.0` (`CanvasChain Symphony`) |
     9→| Supersedes | — |
    10→| Related ADRs | ADR-001 Modular Micro-services, ADR-002 Event Bus |
    11→
    12→---
    13→
    14→## 1. Context
    15→
    16→CanvasChain Symphony aims to be the de-facto playground for experimental digital art on the blockchain.  
    17→Consequently, we must:
    18→
    19→1. Support *multiple* signature schemes—`Ed25519` for mainstream wallets, `BLS12-381` for aggregated votes, and one or more post-quantum candidates (e.g. `Dilithium`, `Falcon`) for future-proofing.
    20→2. Allow *runtime* selection of a scheme for each micro-service (e.g. the **governance** service needs BLS while **composition** might stick with Ed25519 for speed).
    21→3. Offer *hot-swap* capabilities so research collectives can ship cryptographic experiments without forking or recompiling the **entire** chain.
    22→4. Maintain *deterministic* behavior across WASM smart-contracts and native nodes so that consensus is never broken.
    23→5. Remain *auditable* and *testable*—adding new crypto must not impair formal verification or fuzzing pipelines.
    24→
    25→## 2. Decision
    26→
    27→We will implement a **Strategy Pattern** that surfaces an `CryptoSuite` trait across all micro-services.  
    28→A concrete suite is loaded **at startup** according to configuration (environment variable, CLI flag, or chain parameter) and injected via dependency-injection (gRPC metadata and event bus headers propagate the chosen suite).
    29→
    30→Key points:
    31→
    32→* The `CryptoSuite` trait

    13→# CanvasChain Symphony Governance Protocol
    14→
    15→CanvasChain Symphony is governed entirely on-chain through a
    16→token-weighted, stake-weighted process that combines **Proof-of-
    17→Inspiration (PoI)** with a modular on-chain council and an open
    18→referenda system.  
    19→The protocol is implemented in Rust and compiled to WebAssembly
    20→for deterministic smart-contract execution, while the **Governance
    21→Microservice** orchestrates off-chain tasks and gRPC messaging.

     1→```markdown
     2→# CanvasChain Symphony – Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI) Consensus  
     3→*Version 1.3 – Status: **Draft-Stable***  
     4→
     5→---
     6→
     7→## 1  Overview
     8→Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI) is CanvasChain Symphony’s bespoke, stake-weighted, VRF-driven consensus that empowers **composer nodes** to publish on-chain creative updates (“movements”).  
     9→PoI combines:
    10→
    11→* **Delegated Proof-of-Stake (DPoS)** – capital-efficient security and democratic representation.  
    12→* **Verifiable Random Functions (VRF)** – unbiased, publicly verifiable randomness to ∀ participants.  
    13→* **On-chain Inspiration Score** – dynamic modifier fueled by historical creative performance, rewarding nodes that consistently contribute high-value artwork.
    14→
    15→The result is a fast-finality, low-energy, creative-centric protocol optimized for **interactive NFT evolution**.
    16→
    17→---
    18→
    19→## 2  Design Goals
    20→
    21→| Goal                   | Rationale                                               |
    22→|------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------|
    23→| Deterministic yet unpredictable leader election | Prevent censorship & ensure fairness. |
    24→| Human-readable on-chain proofs                 | Facilitate curator audits & gallery integrations. |
    25→| Upgrade-friendly crypto curves (Strategy Pattern) | Support Ed25519, BLS12-381, PQC curves. |
    26→| Slashing for inactivity or malicious art spam | Maintain network & aesthetic integrity. |
    27→
    28→---
    29→
    30→## 3  Terminology
    31→
    32→| Term               | Meaning                                                             |
    33→|--------------------|------------------------------

     2→# CanvasChain Symphony – Marketplace Service
     3→`services/marketplace_service`
     4→
     5→The Marketplace Service powers the primary and secondary exchange of multilayer NFTs
     6→(“Instruments”) on CanvasChain Symphony.  It exposes a gRPC interface for listing,
     7→bidding, buying, and royalty-settlement, publishes domain events on the mesh-bus,
     8→and persists state changes in PostgreSQL using Diesel.  
     9→The service is designed to be **stateless**; business state is maintained in the
    10→database and propagated through events.  
    11→High-throughput order-matching is achieved with an _in-memory order-book_ backed
    12→by **MVCC snapshots** so reads never block writes.

     1→# CanvasChain Symphony – Node Service
     2→
     3→The **Node Service** is the beating heart of CanvasChain Symphony.  
     4→It encapsulates networking, consensus, state-replication, and provides an ergonomic Rust SDK so higher-level micro-services (composition, remixing, marketplace, etc.) can publish transactions or subscribe to real-time events without re-implementing blockchain plumbing.
     5→
     6→---
     7→
     8→## 🧩 Responsibilities
     9→
    10→1. Peer-to-peer networking (libp2p over QUIC + noise)
    11→2. Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI) leader election
    12→3. Transaction / block propagation
    13→4. State–machine replication (+ snapshotting)
    14→5. gRPC façade exposing high-level APIs to the remaining micro-services
    15→6. Event bus bridge (NATS) to fan-out new blocks & governance votes
    16→
    17→---
    18→
    19→## 🔖 Feature Flags
    20→
    21→| Cargo Feature            | Description                                |
    22→|--------------------------|--------------------------------------------|
    23→| `in-memory-db`           | Use an ephemeral RocksDB substitute for tests |
    24→| `bls-signatures`         | Switch from Ed25519 to BLS12-381 curve     |
    25→| `experimental-post-quantum` | Enable Dilithium (PQ-crypto) signatures |
    26→
    27→Activate mutually exclusive curves via:
    28→
    29→```bash
    30→cargo build --release --no-default-features --features bls-signatures
    31→```

     2→# CanvasChain Symphony – Staking Service
     3→
     4→_**Service directory:** `services/staking_service`_  
     5→_**Crate name:** `ccs_staking_service`_  
     6→_**Micro-framework:** [`tonic`](https://github.com/hyperium/tonic) + [`sqlx`](https://github.com/launchbadge/sqlx) + [`tracing`](https://crates.io/crates/tracing)_

     9→_**Crypto provider:** Pluggable through the Strategy Pattern (`Ed25519` → `BLS12-381` → `Dilithium`)_  
    10→
    11→---
    12→## 1. Motivation
    13→
    14→The _Staking Service_ powers the **Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)** consensus layer.  
    15→Participants lock the governance token `$BRUSH` to:
    16→
    17→1. Secure the network and participate in artist election rounds.
    18→2. Earn staking rewards streamed via the DeFi micro-service.
    19→3. Influence trait evolution probabilities of evolving NFTs.
    20→
    21→The service exposes a **gRPC API** and publishes domain events to **NATS** (`staking.events.*`) so that other micro-services (e.g. _governance_, _marketplace_) can react in real-time.

     2→//! Core NFT domain types and evolution/state-machine logic for the
     3→//! CanvasChain Symphony platform.
     4→//!
     5→//! This module purposefully remains *no_std*-friendly (with an opt-in
     6→//! `std` feature for clients that need heap allocation) so it can be
     7→//! reused inside on-chain WASM smart contracts as well as off-chain
     8→//! micro-services.
     9→//!
    10→//! Key design goals:
    11→//! 1. Multi-layer NFTs with independent ownership & royalty streams.
    12→//! 2. Fine-grained state transitions driven by user interaction,
    13→//!    governance votes, staking incentives and DeFi metrics.
    14→//! 3. Pluggable cryptography via Strategy pattern (`SignatureScheme`).
    15→//!
    16→//! NOTE: Heavy business logic such as VRF computation or signature
    17→//! verification lives in dedicated crates (`ccs_cryptography`, …).

62-assistanttool_useRead
63-usertool_resultRead
     1→```rust
     2→//! Node service state–machine
     3→//!
     4→//! This module implements a hierarchical, asynchronous state-machine that
     5→//! drives a single CanvasChain Symphony “conductor” (validator / full node).
     6→//!
     7→//! The public façade is [`NodeStateMachine::spawn`].  Callers provide a
     8→//! configured [`NodeContext`] plus a Tokio `mpsc::Receiver<NodeEvent>` that
     9→//! represents the node’s inbound event bus.  
    10→//!
    11→//! The machine is built around the classic State pattern.  Each state
    12→//! implements [`State`]—an async callback that receives the next event and
    13→//! returns a [`Transition`] indicating whether the machine should:
    14→//!   * stay in the same state
    15→//!   * transition to a new boxed state
    16→//!   * perform a graceful shutdown.
    17→//!
    18→//! Transitions are **total**; all event/state combinations _must_ resolve to a
    19→//! `Transition`, preventing undefined behaviour at runtime.
    20→//!
    21→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    22→//! Conventions & best-practices
    23→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    24→//! • Logging is performed with the `tracing` crate (structured, async-aware).  
    25→//! • All public types derive `Debug` to make tracing easier.  
    26→//! • Errors bubble up using `thiserror::Error` and are logged before causing a
    27→//!   transition into [`StateError`].  
    28→//! • No blocking I/O—everything is fully async.  
    29→//! • `#![deny(clippy::unwrap_used)]` ensures we never `.unwrap()` outside of
    30→//!   tests.  
    31→//!
    32→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    33→//! Example
    
... (truncated)

     6→//! plumbing;  it is meant to be embedded by the service‐layer binary and
     7→//! driven by the surrounding transport / storage adapters.
     8→//!
     9→//! Architectural notes
    10→//! -------------------
    11→//! • State is kept in-memory behind a `RwLock` and checkpointed by the
    12→//!   service into persistent storage (e.g. Postgres, RocksDB) – that part is
    13→//!   out-of-scope here.
    14→//! • Composer selection follows a simplified Proof-of-Inspiration algorithm:
    15→//!      1. Each staker submits a *VRF proof* for a given round‐seed.
    16→//!      2. The hash output is mapped to `[0, 1)`.  The staker wins if
    17→//!         output / stake_total < staker_weight.
    18→//!      3. Ties are broken deterministically by lowest hash.
    19→//! • A Strategy pattern exposes pluggable `VrfProvider`s so that collectives
    20→//!   can experiment with different curves (Ed25519, BLS, PQ, …) without
    21→//!   recompilation of the other micro-services.

## Summary of the Architectural Blueprint

The document covers all required aspects of the F-NFT integration:

- Extended `MultiLayerNft` with fractionalization state tracking
- Defined database schema with 4 new tables: `fractional_tokens`, `fractional_holdings`, `fractional_transfers`, and `buyout_proposals`

### 3. Component-Level Design
- **node_service**: New `NodeEvent` variants for fractionalization, share transfers, and buyouts; new state machine transitions in `StateActive`
- **minting_service**: New `FractionalizeRequest`/`FractionalizeResponse` types and `fractionalize_nft()` method in `NftFactory`
- **marketplace_service**: Extended `Listing` struct with `ListingType::FractionalShares`; new methods for fractional share listings and purchases
- **wallet_service**: Extended `WalletBackend` trait with `fractional_holdings()` and `transfer_shares()` methods
- **governance_service**: Fractional voting power calculation based on share ownership
- **staking_service**: `FractionalStake` tracking for stake-weighted calculations

ARCHITECTURE DECISION RECORDS (ADRs)\n\n#### **ADR 001: Monorepo for Microservices** (Approved, 2024-06-17)\n- **Decision**: Single Git repository with Cargo workspaces instead of 10 independent repos\n- **Rationale**:\n  - Atomic protocol upgrades across services\n  - Unified tooling and linting (`cargo fmt`, `clippy`)\n  - Shared CI cache (~55% build time reduction)\n  - Consistent semantic versioning per crate\n- **Structure**: `crates/` for libraries, `services/` for binaries\n- **Tradeoffs**: Larger repo (~2 GB projected), potential merge conflicts mitigated by conventional commits\n\n#### **ADR 002: gRPC + NATS JetStream** (Accepted, 2023-11-12)\n- **gRPC for Sync RPC**: Service-to-service request/response via `tonic`\n  - Binary protobuf encoding (efficient for large art layers)\n  - Bidirectional streaming for real-time auctions\n  - mTLS security, tower middlewares\n- **NATS JetStream for Async Events**: Publish/subscribe pattern\n  - Subject hierarchy: `domain.context.version.resource.event` (e.g., `nft.composer.v1.artwork.minted`)\n  - Exactly-once semantics for critical events, fire-and-forget for telemetry\n  - Transactional Outbox pattern for at-least-once delivery\n- **Security**: JWT claims propagated via headers, subject ACLs, replay protection via nonces\n\n#### **ADR 003: Pluggable Cryptography Strategy** (Proposed, 2024-05-05)\n- **Pattern**: `CryptoSuite` trait abstraction allowing runtime curve selection\n- **Supported Curves**:\n  - Ed25519 (default, mainstream wallets)\n  - BLS12-381 (threshold signatures, aggregation)\n  - Dilithium (post-quantum, experimental)\n  - Falcon (post-quantum, future)\n- **Implementation**: No-std compatible, crate per algorithm, registry-based loading at startup\n- **Governance**: On-chain allow-list enables/disables suites without hard-forks\n- **Security**: Constant-time verification, key zeroization via `zeroize` crate\n\n---\n\n### 6. contracts\n2. **Proxy Pattern**: Upgradeable smart contract proxies for gas optimization\n3. **Strategy Pattern**: Pluggable crypto curves, fee policies, burn policies\n4. **Observer Pattern**: Event listeners on NFT evolution, governance votes\n5. **State Machine**: NFT lifecycle (Seeded \u2192 Dormant \u2192 Flourishing \u2192 Fragmented \u2192 Archived)\n6. **CQRS**: Command/query separation in marketplace (write to PostgreSQL, read from MVCC snapshots)\n7. **Event Sourcing**: Append-only event log for auditability\n\n---\n\n### 7. NFT STATE MACHINE\n\nFrom `/docs/nft_evolution.md`:\n\n```\nSeeded (newly minted, base DNA + creator signature)\n  \u2193\nDormant (frozen to preserve snapshot)\n  \u2193\nFlourishing (fully mutable, traits append/replace/decay)\n  \u251c\u2192 Evolve* (traits update, once per epoch)\n  \u251c\u2192 Fragmented (split into derivative pieces for remixing)\n  \u2502  \u2514\u2192 Merge (recombine fragmented tokens)\n  \u2514\u2192 Archived (finalized, no transitions possible)\n```\n\n**gRPC Evolution APIs** (from `nft_evolution.proto`):\n- `Inspire(nft_id, vrf_proof)` - Trigger evolution after PoI composer election\n- `Freeze(nft_id, signatures)` - Lock from further changes\n- `Evolve(nft_id, patch)` - Apply layer mutations\n- `Split(nft_id, parts)` - Create fractional pieces\n- `Merge(child_ids[])` - Recombine fragments\n- `Burn(nft_id)` - Irreversible finalization (pluggable burn policy)\n\n---\n\n### 8. PROOF-OF-INSPIRATION (PoI) CONSENSUS\n\nFrom `/docs/proof_of_inspiration.md`:\n\n**Formula for Composer Selection**:\n```\neffective_stake(validator) = \n    base_stake +\n    \u03a3 delegator_balances \u00d7 loyalty_multiplier +\n    inspiration_score \u00d7 \u03b2\n```\n\n**VRF Election Process**:\n1. Seed = H(epoch_randomness || round_no)\n2. VRF output \u2208 [0, 2\u00b2\u2075\u2076) evaluated by each validator\n3. Threshold = 2\u00b2\u2075\u2076 \u00d7 (effective_stake / total_stake)\n4. If VRF_output < threshold \u2192 **Validator wins composer slot**\n\n**Slashing & Rewards**:\n- Double movement (same round): 5% slash + 1 epoch freeze\n- Invalid VRF proof: 100% block reward burned\n- Inactivity (\u2265256 rounds): 1% slash\n- Block rewards: 90% to composer + delegators, 10% to Inspiration Fund\n\n---\n\n### 9. GOVERNANCE PROTOCOL\n\nFrom `/docs/governance_protocol.md`:\n\n**Token**: `$BRUSH` (ERC-20-compatible, stake-weighted voting)\n\n**Proposal Lifecycle**:\n```\nDraft (\u221e) \u2192 Review (48h) \u2192 Voting (72h) \u2192 Enactment (24h) \u2192 Executed/Rejected\n```\n\n**Conviction Voting** (Polkadot-style):\n- 0 blocks: \u00d71 multiplier\n- 80k blocks (~1 week): \u00d72\n- 320k blocks: \u00d73\n- 1.28M blocks: \u00d74\n\n**Smart Contract** (ink! on Substrate):\n- `submit_proposal(ipfs_hash)` - Requires 0.01 BRUSH bond\n- `vote(proposal_id, kind, weight)` - Cast vote with conviction\n- `advance_stage()` - Progress through lifecycle\n- `veto_upgrade()` - \u226530% stake can abort scheduled upgrades\n\n---\n\n### 10. COMMUNICATION & OBSERVABILITY\n\n**Inter-Service Communication**:\n- **gRPC (sync)**: Request/response over Tonic with TLS\n- **NATS JetStream (async)**: Event pub/sub with durable consumers\n- **Transactional Outbox**: Dual-write hazard prevention between DB and event bus\n\n**Observability Stack** (from `docker-compose.yml`):\n- **Logs**: OpenTelemetry + Jaeger tracing\n- **Metrics**: Prometheus exporter on `/metrics` (port 8080 on each service)\n- **Dashboards**: Grafana (port 3000)\n- **Traces**: Tempo (port 4317)\n\n**Health Checks**:\n- All services expose `/health` REST endpoint\n- Docker compose HEALTHCHECK every 10s with 5 retries\n\n---\n\n### 11. DEPLOYMENT & ORCHESTRATION\n\n**Docker Compose Stack** (`docker-compose.yml`):\n- 1\u00d7 NATS event-bus (messaging)\n- 1\u00d7 PostgreSQL 15 (persistence, volumes)\n- 1\u00d7 Substrate consensus-node (RPC on 9944, P2P on 30333)\n- 8\u00d7 Microservices (REST on 6001-6008, gRPC on 7001-7008)\n- 4\u00d7 Observability (Prometheus, Grafana, Tempo)\n\n**Network**: All services on single bridge network `canvaschain`\n\n**Environment Variables** (shared across all services):\n```bash\nRUST_LOG=info,hyper=warn,tower=warn\nEVENT_BUS_URL=nats://event-bus:4222\nDATABASE_URL=postgres://canvas:canvas@db:5432/canvas\nCONSENSUS_NODE_URL=http://consensus-node:9944\nOTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT=http://tempo:4317\n```\n\n---\n\n### 12. WORKSPACE DEPENDENCIES (from `Cargo.toml`)\n\n**Core async runtime**:\n- `tokio` v1.32 (multi-threaded)\n\n**gRPC stack**:\n- `tonic` v0.9 (async gRPC server)\n- `prost` v0.11 (Protobuf serialization)\n\n**Serialization**:\n- `serde` v1.0, `serde_json` v1.0\n\n**Error handling**:\n- `anyhow` v1.0, `thiserror` v1.0\n\n**Event bus**:\n- `nats` v0.23 (async NATS client)\n\n**Cryptography**:\n- `ed25519-dalek` v1.0.1 (default)\n- `blst` v0.3 (optional BLS)\n- `pqcrypto` v0.7.1 (optional post-quantum)\n\n**Logging & tracing**:\n- `tracing` v0.1, `tracing-subscriber` v0.3\n\n**Feature Flags**:\n- `wallet_integration` (default)\n- `token_management` (default)\n- `governance`, `defi_protocols`, `smart_contracts`\n- `bls`, `post_quantum` (experimental)\n\n---\n\n### 13. "     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192# CanvasChain Symphony \u2013 Architecture Guide  \n     3\u2192Project: `rust_blockchain_nft_expert_071` (codename *CanvasChain Symphony*)  \n     4\u2192Version: 0.8.0-alpha\n     5\u2192\n     6\u2192> \u201cEvery block is a bar; every transaction a note.\u201d \u2013 The CanvasChain Collective\n     7\u2192\n     8\u2192---\n     9\u2192\n    10\u2192## 1. High-Level Overview\n    11\u2192CanvasChain Symphony is a constellation of **10 Rust micro-services** that collectively operate a modular blockchain-NFT platform for generative and interactive digital art.\n    12\u2192\n    13\u2192* Each \u201cmovement\u201d (feature domain) is an **independent service** with a bounded context.  \n    14\u2192* Services communicate via **gRPC** for request/response semantics and a **NATS JetStream** event bus for pub/sub and CQRS projections.  \n    15\u2192* A custom consensus algorithm, **Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)**, blends stake-weighted VRF elections with curator voting to periodically select a \u201cComposer Node\u201d that may commit a generative-art update.\n    16\u2192\n    17\u2192```\n    18\u2192\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      gRPC        \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n    19\u2192\u2502  Wallet Service  \u2502\u25c0\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u25b6\u2502  Governance Svc  \u2502\n    20\u2192\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518                 \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n    21\u2192        \u25b2     \u25b2                               \u25b2\n 2. Micro-service Topology\n    32\u2192\n    33\u2192| Service           | Domain                           | Patterns Used                          |\n    34\u2192|-------------------|----------------------------------|----------------------------------------|\n    35\u2192| `wallet`          | Key management, authentication   | Strategy (crypto curves)               |\n    36\u2192| `governance`      | On-chain DAO voting             | State Machine, Observer                |\n    37\u2192| `minting`         | NFT creation / composition       | Factory, Proxy                         |\n    38\u2192| `remix`           | Trait evolution & layering       | State Machine, Observer                |\n    39\u2192| `marketplace`     | Orderbook & royalties            | Event-Driven, Proxy                    |\n    40\u2192| `staking`         | DeFi incentives / PoI weights    | Strategy, Event-Driven                 |\n    41\u2192| `discovery`       | Metadata & search index          | CQRS, Event Sourcing                   |\n    42\u2192| `composer`        | PoI candidate & block producer   | Strategy, State Machine                |\n    43\u2192| `oracle`          | Off-chain randomness / VRF       | Strategy                               |\n    44\u2192| `monitor`         | Telemetry & health               | Observer                               |\n    45\u2192\n    46\u2192---\n    47\u2192\n    48\u2192## 3. Inter-Service Communication\n    49\u2192\n    50\u2192### 3.1 gRPC Interface Example (Tonic)\n    51\u2192\n    52\u2192```rust\n    53\u2192// crates/minting/src/api.rs\n    54\u2192use tonic::{Request, Response, Status};\n    55\u2192use uuid::Uuid;\n    56\u2192\n    57\u2192tonic::include_proto!(\"canvaschain.minting\");\n    58\u2192\n    59\u2192#[derive(Debug, Default)]\n    60\u2192pub struct MintingApi;\n    61\u2192\n    62\u2192#[tonic::async_trait]\n    63\u2192impl minting_server::Minting for MintingApi {\n    64\u2192    async fn compose_nft(\n    65\u2192        &self,\n    66\u2192        req: Request<ComposeRequest>,\n    67\u2192    ) -> Result<Response<ComposeReply>, Status> {\n    68\u2192        let payload = req.into_inner();\n    69\u2192        let nft_id = Uuid::new_v4();\n    70\u2192\n    71\u2192        // Business logic delegates to domain layer.\n    72\u2192        domain::compose_nft(&payload)\n    73\u2192            .await\n    74\u2192            .map_err(|e| Status::internal(e.to_string()))?;\n    75\u2192\n    76\u2192        Ok(Response::new(ComposeReply { nft_id: nft_id.to_string() }))\n    77\u2192    }\n    78\u2192}\n    79\u2192```\n    80\u2192\n    81\u2192### 3.2 Event Bus Contract\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192All domain events are versioned and serialized with **Prost** + **Serde**.  \n    84\u2192Subject naming convention: `canvas.<service>.<aggregate>.<event>`.\n    85\u2192\n    86\u2192```rust\n    87\u2192// events/src/lib.rs\n    88\u2192use chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\n    89\u2192use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n    90\u2192\n    91\u2192pub const SCHEMA_VERSION: &str = \"v1\";\n    92\u2192\n    93\u2192#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n    94\u2192#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\n    95\u2192pub enum Event {\n    96\u2192    NftComposed(NftComposed),\n    97\u2192    BidPlaced(BidPlaced),\n    98\u2192    GovernanceVoteCast(VoteCast),\n    99\u2192    // ...\n   100\u2192}\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n   103\u2192pub struct NftComposed {\n   104\u2192    pub nft_id: String,\n   105\u2192    pub composer: String,\n   106\u2192    pub timestamp: DateTime<Utc>,\n   107\u2192    pub layers: Vec<String>,\n   108\u2192}\n   109\u2192```\n   110\u2192\n   111\u2192---\n   112\u2192\n   113\u2192## 4. Core Design Pattern Implementations\n   114\u2192\n   115\u2192### 4.1 Factory Pattern \u2013 NFT Instrument Factory\n   116\u2192\n   117\u2192```rust\n   118\u2192// crates/minting/src/factory.rs\n   119\u2192use super::{error::FactoryError, instruments::*};\n   120\u2192\n   121\u2192pub trait InstrumentFactory: Send + Sync {\n   122\u2192    fn spawn(&self, spec: InstrumentSpec) -> Result<Box<dyn Instrument>, FactoryError>;\n   123\u2192}\n   124\u2192\n   125\u2192pub struct DefaultFactory;\n   126\u2192\n   127\u2192impl InstrumentFactory for DefaultFactory {\n   128\u2192    fn spawn(&self, spec: InstrumentSpec) -> Result<Box<dyn Instrument>, FactoryError> {\n   129\u2192        match spec.kind.as_str() {\n   130\u2192            \"Audio\" => Ok(Box::new(AudioInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n   131\u2192            \"Visual\" => Ok(Box::new(VisualInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n   132\u2192            \"Haptic\" => Ok(Box::new(HapticInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n   133\u2192            _ => Err(FactoryError::UnsupportedKind(spec.kind)),\n   134\u2192        }\n   135\u2192    }\n   136\u2192}\n   137\u2192```\n   138\u2192\n   139\u2192### 4.2 Proxy Pattern \u2013 Upgradable Smart Contract Proxy\n   140\u2192\n   141\u2192```rust\n   142\u2192// smart_contracts/proxy/src/lib.rs\n   143\u2192use ink::env::call::{build_call, utils::ReturnType};\n   144\u2192use ink::prelude::vec::Vec;\n   145\u2192use ink::primitives::Clear;\n   146\u2192\n   147\u2192#[ink::contract]\n   148\u2192mod proxy {\n   149\u2192    use super::*;\n   150\u2192\n   151\u2192    #[ink(storage)]\n   152\u2192    pub struct Proxy {\n   153\u2192        implementation: AccountId,\n   154\u2192        admin: AccountId,\n   155\u2192    }\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192    impl Proxy {\n   158\u2192        #[ink(constructor)]\n   159\u2192        pub fn new(implementation: AccountId) -> Self {\n   160\u2192            Self { implementation, admin: Self::env().caller() }\n   161\u2192        }\n   162\u2192\n   163\u2192        #[ink(message)]\n   164\u2192        pub fn upgrade(&mut self, new_impl: AccountId) {\n   165\u2192            assert_eq!(self.env().caller(), self.admin);\n   166\u2192            self.implementation = new_impl;\n   167\u2192        }\n   168\u2192\n   169\u2192        #[ink(message, payable, selector = _)]\n   170\u2192        pub fn fallback(&self) -> Vec<u8> {\n   171\u2192            let result = build_call::<ink::env::DefaultEnvironment>()\n   172\u2192                .call(self.implementation)\n   173\u2192                .transferred_value(Self::env().transferred_value())\n   174\u2192                .exec_input(ink::env::call::ExecutionInput::new(Self::env().selector()).push_arg(Self::env().input()))\n   175\u2192                .returns::<ReturnType<Vec<u8>>>()\n   176\u2192                .fire()\n   177\u2192                .expect(\"proxy call failed\");\n   178\u2192            result\n   179\u2192        }\n   180\u2192    }\n   181\u2192}\n   182\u2192```\n   183\u2192\n   184\u2192### 4.3 Observer Pattern \u2013 Trait Evolution Listener\n   185\u2192\n   186\u2192```rust\n   187\u2192// crates/remix/src/observer.rs\n   188\u2192use async_nats::Subscriber;\n   189\u2192use tracing::{debug, error};\n   190\u2192\n   191\u2192pub async fn start_trait_observer(sub: Subscriber) -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n   192\u2192    while let Some(msg) = sub.next().await {\n   193\u2192        match serde_json::from_slice::<events::Event>(&msg.payload) {\n   194\u2192            Ok(events::Event::NftComposed(event)) => {\n   195\u2192                debug!(\"Handling NftComposed: {:?}\", event);\n   196\u2192                // Trigger trait evolution workflow.\n   197\u2192            }\n   198\u2192            Ok(_) => {},\n   199\u2192            Err(e) => error!(error = %e, \"Failed to deserialize event\"),\n   200\u2192        }\n   201\u2192    }\n   202\u2192    Ok(())\n   203\u2192}\n   204\u2192```\n   205\u2192\n   206\u2192### 4.4 State Machine \u2013 NFT Lifecycle\n   207\u2192\n   208\u2192```rust\n   209\u2192// domain/src/state_machine.rs\n   210\u2192use crate::error::StateError;\n   211\u2192use strum::{Display, EnumIter, EnumString};\n   212\u2192\n   213\u2192#[derive(Clone, Debug, EnumIter, EnumString, Display, PartialEq, Eq)]\n   214\u2192pub enum NftState {\n   215\u2192    Draft,\n   216\u2192    Minted,\n   217\u2192    Listed,\n   218\u2192    Locked,\n   219\u2192    Transferred,\n   220\u2192}\n   221\u2192\n   222\u2192impl NftState {\n   223\u2192    pub fn transit(self, event: &str) -> Result<NftState, StateError> {\n   224\u2192        use NftState::*;\n   225\u2192        Ok(match (self, event) {\n   226\u2192            (Draft, \"mint\") => Minted,\n   227\u2192            (Minted, \"list\") => Listed,\n   228\u2192            (Listed, \"lock\") => Locked,\n   229\u2192            (Locked, \"transfer\") => Transferred,\n   230\u2192            _ => return Err(StateError::InvalidTransition),\n   231\u2192        })\n   232\u2192    }\n   233\u2192}\n   234\u2192```\n   235\u2192\n   236\u2192### 4.5 Strategy Pattern \u2013 Pluggable Cryptographic Curves\n   237\u2192\n   238\u2192```rust\n   239\u2192// crates/crypto/src/strategy.rs\n   240\u2192use ed25519_dalek as ed25519;\n   241\u2192use bls_signatures::{PrivateKey as BlsPriv, Serialize as _};\n   242\u2192use pqcrypto_dilithium::dilithium2;\n   243\u2192\n   244\u2192pub trait SigningStrategy: Send + Sync {\n   245\u2192    fn sign(&self, msg: &[u8]) -> Vec<u8>;\n   246\u2192    fn verify(&self, msg: &[u8], sig: &[u8]) -> bool;\n   247\u2192}\n   248\u2192\n   249\u2192pub struct Ed25519Strategy(ed25519::Keypair);\n   250\u2192pub struct BlsStrategy(BlsPriv);\n   251\u2192pub struct DilithiumStrategy(dilithium2::keypair::PublicKey, dilithium2::keypair::SecretKey);\n   252\u2192\n   253\u2192impl SigningStrategy for Ed25519Strategy {\n   254\u2192    fn sign(&self, msg: &[u8]) -> Vec<u8> {\n   255\u2192        self.0.sign(msg).to_bytes().to_vec()\n   256\u2192    }\n   257\u2192    fn verify(&self, msg: &[u8], sig: &[u8]) -> bool {\n   258\u2192        ed25519::Signature::from_bytes(sig)\n   259\u2192            .and_then(|s| self.0.verify(msg, &s).map(|_| ()))\n   260\u2192            .is_ok()\n   261\u2192    }\n   262\u2192}\n   263\u2192\n   264\u2192// Implementations for BlsStrategy and DilithiumStrategy omitted for brevity.\n   265\u2192```\n   266\u2192\n   267\u2192---\n   268\u2192\n   269\u2192## 5. Consensus \u2013 Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)\n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192```rust\n   272\u2192// consensus/src/poi.rs\n   273\u2192use rand_core::OsRng;\n   274\u2192use vrf::{openssl::CipherSuite, VRF};\n   275\u2192\n   276\u2192pub struct Candidate {\n   277\u2192    pub node_id: String,\n   278\u2192    pub stake: u128,\n   279\u2192    pub curator_score: u64,\n   280\u2192}\n   281\u2192\n   282\u2192pub fn elect_composer(candidates: &[Candidate], epoch: u64) -> Option<String> {\n   283\u2192    let total_weight: f64 = candidates\n   284\u2192        .iter()\n   285\u2192        .map(|c| (c.stake as f64) * 0.8 + (c.curator_score as f64) * 0.2)\n   286\u2192        .sum();\n   287\u2192\n   288\u2192    let vrf_seed = derive_epoch_seed(epoch);\n   289\u2192    let mut highest = None;\n   290\u2192    let mut highest_score = 0f64;\n   291\u2192\n   292\u2192    for c in candidates {\n   293\u2192        // VRF output \u2208 [0,1)\n   294\u2192        let vrf_out = vrf_draw(&c.node_id, vrf_seed);\n   295\u2192        let weighted = vrf_out * ((c.stake as f64) + 1.0).ln();\n   296\u2192\n   297\u2192        let final_score = weighted / total_weight;\n   298\u2192        if final_score > highest_score {\n   299\u2192            highest_score = final_score;\n   300\u2192            highest = Some(c.node_id.clone());\n   301\u2192        }\n   302\u2192    }\n   303\u2192    highest\n   304\u2192}\n   305\u2192\n   306\u2192fn vrf_draw(node_id: &str, seed: [u8; 32]) -> f64 {\n   307\u2192    let mut csprng = OsRng;\n   308\u2192    let key = CipherSuite::generate_keypair(&mut csprng);\n   309\u2192    let vrf = key\n   310\u2192        .0\n   311\u2192        .prove(&seed)\n   312\u2192        .expect(\"VRF prove failed\")\n   313\u2192        .hash::<sha2::Sha256>();\n   314\u2192    let num = u128::from_le_bytes(vrf[0..16].try_into().unwrap());\n   315\u2192    (num as f64) / (u128::MAX as f64)\n   316\u2192}\n   317\u2192\n   318\u2192fn derive_epoch_seed(epoch: u64) -> [u8; 32] {\n   319\u2192    use sha2::{Digest, Sha256};\n   320\u2192    let mut hasher = Sha256::new();\n   321\u2192    hasher.update(epoch.to_le_bytes());\n   322\u2192    hasher.finalize().into()\n   323\u2192}\n   324\u2192```\n   325\u2192\n   326\u2192---\n   327\u2192\n   328\u2192## 6. Error Handling & Observability\n   329\u2192\n   330\u2192* `thiserror` for domain-level error enums.  \n   331\u2192* `anyhow` at service boundaries for rich context.  \n   332\u2192* `tracing` with OpenTelemetry exporters for logs, metrics and spans.  \n   333\u2192* Circuit-breaker middleware on all gRPC clients using `tower::limit::ConcurrencyLimitFuture`.\n   334\u2192\n   335\u2192---\n   336\u2192\n   337\u2192## 7. Security Considerations\n   338\u2192\n   339\u21921. Hardware-backed key storage (`yubihsm` feature flag).  \n   340\u21922. Merkle-proof inclusion for off-chain metadata.  \n   341\u21923. Re-entrancy guards on Ink! contracts via `non_reentrant` macro.  \n   342\u21924. Formal verification pipeline (K-framework specs in `/formal_specs`).\n   343\u2192\n   344\u2192---\n   345\u2192\n   346\u2192## 8. "     1\u2192# 001 \u2013 Adopt a Monorepo for Rust Microservices\n     2\u2192\n     3\u2192Status: **Approved**  \n     4\u2192Date: 2024-06-17  \n     5\u2192Tags: `repository`, `dev\u2010experience`, `ci/cd`, `rust`, `microservices`\n     6\u2192\n     7\u2192---\n     8\u2192\n     9\u2192## Context\n    10\u2192\n    11\u2192CanvasChain Symphony orchestrates ten specialized Rust microservices\u2014`composition`, `minting`, `remixing`, `marketplace`, `royalty`, `wallet`, `governance`, `token-management`, `defi`, and `orchestrator`.  \n    12\u2192Early prototypes lived in independent Git repositories. While this respected bounded context, it created friction:\n    13\u2192\n    14\u2192* **Version skew**: cross-service protocol buffers, domain types and cryptographic primitives (e.g., our pluggable `CurveStrategy`) drifted, forcing tedious cherry-picks.\n    15\u2192* **Atomic evolution**: a change to a shared crate (e.g., `canvas-chain-primitives`) required synchronized releases across repos; partial updates risked network halts.\n    16\u2192* **CI\ud83d\udcb0**: each repo ran its own CI minutes; caching was duplicated and expensive.\n    17\u2192* **Dev onboarding**: cloning ten repos, wiring SSH deploy keys and remembering divergent release processes slowed contributors.\n    18\u2192\n    19\u2192Rust\u2019s native support for [Cargo workspaces](https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch14-03-cargo-workspaces.html) and our need for atomic, protocol-grade versioning make a monorepo attractive.\n    20\u2192\n    21\u2192## Decision\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192We will:\n    24\u2192\n    25\u21921. Move all Rust microservices, shared crates (`*-primitives`, `*-proto`, etc.) and infrastructure scripts into a single repository named `canvaschain-symphony`.\n    26\u21922. Organize code using Cargo workspaces:\n    27\u2192\n    28\u2192```\n    29\u2192canvaschain-symphony/\n    30\u2192\u251c\u2500\u2500 Cargo.toml            # root workspace manifest\n    31\u2192\u251c\u2500\u2500 crates/\n    32\u2192\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 primitives/\n    33\u2192\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 proto/\n    34\u2192\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 curve-strategy/\n    35\u2192\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 \u2026\n    36\u2192\u2514\u2500\u2500 services/\n    37\u2192    \u251c\u2500\u2500 composition/\n    38\u2192    \u251c\u2500\u2500 minting/\n    39\u2192    \u2514\u2500\u2500 \u2026\n    40\u2192```\n    41\u2192\n    42\u21923. Keep **one** `main` branch protected by mandatory checks. Feature work occurs in PRs with review from at least one other domain owner.\n    43\u21924. Maintain **semantic versioning per crate** using `cargo-release`. A change to `canvaschain-primitives` bumps only that crate, but CI blocks merging unless all dependants still compile.\n    44\u21925. Employ a top-level `Makefile.toml` (cargo-make) for common developer tasks (`make db`, `make dev-up`, etc.).\n    45\u21926. Leverage GitHub Actions\u2019 shared cache: incremental build artifacts (~650 MB) are reused across microservices, cutting CI by ~55 %.\n    46\u21927. Use code-owners to preserve microservice boundaries:\n    47\u2192\n    48\u2192```\n    49\u2192# CODEOWNERS\n    50\u2192/services/composition/ @art-algo @orchestrator\n    51\u2192/services/marketplace/ @defi-team\n    52\u2192/crates/primitives/ @core-protocol\n    53\u2192```\n    54\u2192\n    55\u2192## Consequences\n    56\u2192\n    57\u2192### Positive\n    58\u2192\n    59\u2192* **Atomic protocol upgrades** across services\u2014e.g., adding a new VRF proof to `ProofOfInspiration` requires one PR, one commit hash.\n    60\u2192* Unified **tooling and linting** (`cargo fmt`, `cargo clippy`, `cargo udeps`, `cargo deny`).\n    61\u2192* **Consistent release pipeline**: `cargo make release` builds Docker images for all changed services with version tags derived from Git metadata.\n    62\u2192* **Simplified local dev**: `make dev-up` spins up all services via `docker-compose`, seeded with testnet state.\n    63\u2192* Easier **refactoring**: `cargo fix --workspace` can propagate changes instantly.\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192### Negative\n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192* Repo size grows quickly (projected 2 GB in 18 months). We will enforce **Git LFS** for large fixtures (e.g., generative art sample sets).\n    68\u2192* Potential for **cross-team merge conflicts**; mitigated by conventional commits and smaller PR scope.\n    69\u2192* Accidental **hidden coupling**; owners must respect microservice boundaries and avoid reaching into sibling domains.\n    70\u2192\n    71\u2192### Mitigations\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192* **Bazel remote cache** is on our roadmap for even faster incremental builds.\n    74\u2192* Introduce `cargo hack` to run feature-matrix tests only on changed crates.\n    75\u2192* Quarterly **module sociability reviews** to detect leakage in service boundaries.\n    76\u2192\n    77\u2192---\n    78\u2192\n    79\u2192## Cargo Workspace Manifest (excerpt)\n    80\u2192\n    81\u2192```toml\n    82\u2192[workspace]\n    83\u2192members = [\n    84\u2192    \"crates/primitives\",\n    85\u2192    \"crates/proto\",\n    86\u2192    \"crates/curve-strategy\",\n    87\u2192    \"services/composition\",\n    88\u2192    \"services/minting\",\n    89\u2192    \"services/remixing\",\n    90\u2192    \"services/marketplace\",\n    91\u2192    \"services/royalty\",\n    92\u2192    \"services/wallet\",\n    93\u2192    \"services/governance\",\n    94\u2192    \"services/token-management\",\n    95\u2192    \"services/defi\",\n    96\u2192    \"services/orchestrator\",\n    97\u2192]\n    98\u2192\n    99\u2192[workspace.dependencies]\n   100\u2192tokio          = { version = \"1.37\", features = [\"rt-multi-thread\", \"macros\"] }\n   101\u2192prost          = \"0.12\"\n   102\u2192tonic          = { version = \"0.11\", features = [\"transport\"] }\n   103\u2192tracing        = \"0.1\"\n   104\u2192anyhow         = \"1\"\n   105\u2192thiserror      = \"1\"\n   106\u2192serde          = { version = \"1\", features = [\"derive\"] }\n   107\u2192async-trait    = \"0.1\"\n   108\u2192```\n   109\u2192\n   110\u2192---\n   111\u2192\n   112\u2192## Adoption Plan\n   113\u2192\n   114\u21921. Freeze external repos; merge them into the new `canvaschain-symphony` monorepo preserving commit history (`git subtree add`).\n   115\u21922. Update CI to run workspace-aware commands (`cargo test --workspace`).\n   116\u21923. Notify the community via Discord, update contributor docs, schedule \u201cdev-env day\u201d to migrate local clones.\n   117\u21924. Archive old repositories as read-only.\n   118\u2192\n   119\u2192---\n   120\u2192\n   121\u2192## References\n   122\u2192\n   123\u2192* RFC-0396 \u2013 \u201cCargo Workspaces in Large Rust Projects\u201d  \n   124\u2192* ADR-004 \u2013 \u201cEvent Bus over gRPC\u201d  \n   125\u2192* Google SRE Book, Chap. 5 \u2013 \u201cMonorepos at Scale\u201d\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"

"     1\u2192# ADR 002: gRPC for Service-to-Service RPC and NATS Event Bus for Asynchronous Messaging\n     2\u2192\n     3\u2192Date: 2023-11-12  \n     4\u2192Status: Accepted  \n     5\u2192Supersedes: \u2014  \n     6\u2192Superseded by: \u2014  \n     7\u2192Authors: Core Architecture Team (CanvasChain Symphony)\n     8\u2192\n     9\u2192---\n    10\u2192\n    11\u2192## 1. Context\n    12\u2192\n    13\u2192CanvasChain Symphony is composed of ten autonomous Rust micro-services\u2014`composer`, `minter`, `remixer`, `market-maker`, `royalty-streamer`, etc. Each service is owned and deployed independently yet must inter-operate to deliver end-to-end user flows. Two communication patterns are required:\n    14\u2192\n    15\u21921. **Request / Response (RPC)**  \n    16\u2192   Example: the `market-maker` service must synchronously query `token-registry` for the current royalty split before quoting a swap.\n    17\u2192\n    18\u21922. **Publish / Subscribe (Eventing)**  \n    19\u2192   Example: the `governance` service votes on a \u201cmovement\u201d that triggers the `composer` to mint the next artwork. Every interested service (`gallery-renderer`, `royalty-streamer`, `analytics`) must react to the same chain event without tight coupling.\n    20\u2192\n    21\u2192Key non-functional drivers:\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192* **Performance:** high throughput, low latency, binary payloads (art layers can be large).\n    24\u2192* **Language Inter-op:** we anticipate plug-ins in Python (ML models), WASM (browser previews), and potentially Solidity-compiled bindings.\n    25\u2192* **Back-Pressure & Delivery Guarantees:** at-least-once delivery for critical NFT state transitions, but fire-and-forget for analytics streams.\n    26\u2192* **Security:** end-to-end encryption (mTLS), pluggable authN/authZ compatible with our wallet integration.\n    27\u2192\n    28\u2192---\n    29\u2192\n    30\u2192## 2. Decision\n    31\u2192\n    32\u21921. **gRPC** will be adopted for all synchronous, intra-cluster RPC calls.  \n    33\u21922. **NATS JetStream** will be adopted as the event bus for asynchronous, pub/sub communication.\n    34\u2192\n    35\u2192---\n    36\u2192\n    37\u2192## 3. Rationale\n    38\u2192\n    39\u2192### Why gRPC?\n    40\u2192\n    41\u2192* **IDL-First Development.** Protocol Buffers give us a single source of truth for message schemas in Rust, Python, TypeScript, etc.  \n    42\u2192* **Streaming Support.** Bidirectional streams map naturally to live trait evolution and real-time auction bidding.  \n    43\u2192* **Excellent Rust Ecosystem.** `tonic` provides async/await support, tower middlewares, and first-class mTLS.  \n    44\u2192* **Efficient Binary Encoding.** Artwork layers are sent as deltas or binary blobs; Protobuf minimizes overhead compared to JSON.  \n    45\u2192\n    46\u2192### Why NATS JetStream?\n    47\u2192\n    48\u2192* **Lightweight & Cloud-Native.** Simple single-binary, horizontal-scaling suitability for micro-k8s clusters.  \n    49\u2192* **Exactly-Once Semantics (Opt-In).** JetStream can persist critical events (e.g., ownership transfers) while still allowing fire-and-forget subjects for telemetry.  \n    50\u2192* **Observable.** Built-in tracing, ad-hocs, and integration with Grafana Promtail for distributed tracing.  \n    51\u2192* **Secure Subjects.** Supports leaf-nodes and account isolation, enabling multi-tenant \u201cartist pools.\u201d  \n    52\u2192* **Rust Client Quality.** `nats.rs` offers async, typed-structured messages and JetStream KV for on-chain state mirroring.\n    53\u2192\n    54\u2192### Alternatives Considered\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192| Option                    | Pros                                              | Cons                                                      |\n    57\u2192|---------------------------|---------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|\n    58\u2192| REST/JSON over HTTP/2     | Ubiquitous, easy to debug                         | Verbose payloads, no streaming, manual schema evolution   |\n    59\u2192| GraphQL Federation        | Flexible querying                                 | Overkill for service-to-service calls, N + 1 traps        |\n    60\u2192| Apache Kafka              | Durable, massive throughput                       | Operationally heavy, zookeeper (or KRaft) complexity      |\n    61\u2192| RabbitMQ                  | Mature, routing patterns                          | Lower raw throughput, heavier client libs for WASM        |\n    62\u2192| ZeroMQ                    | Embedded-style speed                              | No central broker, discovery challenges                   |\n    63\u2192\n    64\u2192gRPC + NATS best satisfied the combined performance, ergonomics, and operational simplicity we need.\n    65\u2192\n    66\u2192---\n    67\u2192\n    68\u2192## 4. Detailed Design\n    69\u2192\n    70\u2192### 4.1 gRPC Service Definitions\n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192Service contracts live in `proto/` and are versioned via Git tags. An excerpt:\n    73\u2192\n    74\u2192```protobuf\n    75\u2192syntax = \"proto3\";\n    76\u2192\n    77\u2192package canvaschain.market.v1;\n    78\u2192\n    79\u2192service RoyaltyService {\n    80\u2192  // Returns the royalty split for a given NFT\n    81\u2192  rpc GetRoyaltyInfo(GetRoyaltyInfoRequest) returns (GetRoyaltyInfoResponse) {\n    82\u2192    option (google.api.http) = {\n    83\u2192      get: \"/v1/royalty/{token_id}\"\n    84\u2192    };\n    85\u2192  }\n    86\u2192}\n    87\u2192\n    88\u2192message GetRoyaltyInfoRequest {\n    89\u2192  uint64 token_id = 1;\n    90\u2192}\n    91\u2192\n    92\u2192message GetRoyaltyInfoResponse {\n    93\u2192  repeated Split split = 1;\n    94\u2192}\n    95\u2192\n    96\u2192message Split {\n    97\u2192  string recipient = 1;         // wallet address\n    98\u2192  uint32 share_bps   = 2;       // basis points\n    99\u2192}\n   100\u2192```\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192Rust code is generated with `prost` + `tonic_build`:\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192```rust\n   105\u2192// build.rs\n   106\u2192fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {\n   107\u2192    tonic_build::configure()\n   108\u2192        .build_server(true)\n   109\u2192        .build_client(true)\n   110\u2192        .out_dir(\"src/proto\")\n   111\u2192        .compile(&[\n   112\u2192            \"proto/canvaschain/market/v1/royalty_service.proto\",\n   113\u2192        ], &[\"proto\"])?;\n   114\u2192    Ok(())\n   115\u2192}\n   116\u2192```\n   117\u2192\n   118\u2192### 4.2 gRPC Infrastructure Patterns\n   119\u2192\n   120\u2192* **Interceptors:** Uniform wallet-signature validation (`x-canvas-sig`), request tracing (OpenTelemetry).  \n   121\u2192* **Resilience:** `tower::retry::Retry` with exponential backoff for transient failures.  \n   122\u2192* **Codegen Regeneration:** GitHub Action enforces that `cargo build --workspace` fails if `proto/` drift is detected.\n   123\u2192\n   124\u2192### 4.3 NATS JetStream Topology\n   125\u2192\n   126\u2192Subject naming convention: `domain.context.version.resource.event`  \n   127\u2192Example: `nft.composer.v1.artwork.minted`\n   128\u2192\n   129\u2192* **Streams:**  \n   130\u2192  * `core.events` \u2013 all critical state changes, storage TTL = 365 d, ack = explicit  \n   131\u2192  * `telemetry.metrics` \u2013 non-critical stats, storage TTL = 1 d, ack = none  \n   132\u2192* **Consumers:**  \n   133\u2192  * Durable pull consumer per microservice (`composer_core`, `gallery_renderer`, \u2026).  \n   134\u2192  * Ephemeral consumers for CLI tools and data scientists.\n   135\u2192\n   136\u2192Rust subscription example:\n   137\u2192\n   138\u2192```rust\n   139\u2192let event: MintedEvent = jetstream\n   140\u2192    .get_stream(\"core.events\")?\n   141\u2192    .create_consumer(ConsumerConfig {\n   142\u2192        durable_name: Some(\"gallery_renderer\".to_string()),\n   143\u2192        filter_subject: \"nft.composer.v1.artwork.minted\".into(),\n   144\u2192        deliver_policy: DeliverPolicy::All,\n   145\u2192        ack_policy: AckPolicy::Explicit,\n   146\u2192        ..Default::default()\n   147\u2192    })?\n   148\u2192    .messages()?\n   149\u2192    .next()\n   150\u2192    .await?\n   151\u2192    .unwrap()\n   152\u2192    .deserialize()?;\n   153\u2192```\n   154\u2192\n   155\u2192### 4.4 Transactional Outbox Pattern\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192To avoid dual-write hazards between the PostgreSQL command side and the event bus, each service implements the **Transactional Outbox** pattern. A reliable background task (`tokio::spawn`) pulls unsent events, publishes to NATS, and marks them dispatched. This guarantees at-least-once delivery even if the service crashes mid-transaction.\n   158\u2192\n   159\u2192![Transactional Outbox Diagram](../../design/diagrams/transactional_outbox.png)\n   160\u2192\n   161\u2192---\n   162\u2192\n   163\u2192## 5. Security Considerations\n   164\u2192\n   165\u2192* **mTLS Everywhere:** Shared SPIFFE IDs (`spiffe://canvaschain/{service}`) issued by cert-manager.  \n   166\u2192* **Subject ACLs:** Only the `composer` may publish on `nft.composer.*`; others read-only.  \n   167\u2192* **JWT Claims:** gRPC headers leverage short-lived JWTs signed by the `auth` service, propagated via NATS headers for traceability.  \n   168\u2192* **Replay Protection:** Nonces + timestamp fields in all state-changing Protobuf messages.\n   169\u2192\n   170\u2192---\n   171\u2192\n   172\u2192## 6. Consequences\n   173\u2192\n   174\u2192### Positive\n   175\u2192\n   176\u2192* Consistent developer experience across sync and async messaging.\n   177\u2192* Performance-optimized binary encoding keeps latency < 15 ms P99 inside the same AZ.\n   178\u2192* Pluggable structure: any service can be rewritten in another language with minimal friction.\n   179\u2192* Observability is unified via OpenTelemetry exporters for `tonic` and `nats.rs`.\n   180\u2192\n   181\u2192### Negative / Trade-offs\n   182\u2192\n   183\u2192* Learning curve for contributors unfamiliar with Protocol Buffers.\n   184\u2192* Operationally, we must maintain a NATS cluster (RAFT group) in addition to the Postgres DB.\n   185\u2192* Protobuf evolution requires backward-compatibility discipline to avoid breaking older miners.\n   186\u2192\n   187\u2192---\n   188\u2192\n   189\u2192## 7. Measures of Success\n   190\u2192\n   191\u21921. End-to-end mint-to-marketplace latency \u2264 200 ms on staging.\n   192\u21922. Zero lost critical events during chaos-testing (`chaos-nats` network partitions).\n   193\u21923. Successful inter-op PoC of Python `remixer` plugin subscribing to `nft.*` events.\n   194\u2192\n   195\u2192---\n   196\u2192\n   197\u2192## 8. References\n   198\u2192\n   199\u2192* NATS JetStream Design: https://docs.nats.io/jetstream  \n   200\u2192* tonic gRPC Rust Library: https://github.com/hyperium/tonic  \n   201\u2192* \u201cTransactional Outbox\u201d by Pat Helland: https://microservices.io/patterns/data/transactional-outbox.html  \n   202\u2192* gRPC Security Best Practices: https://grpc.io/docs/guides/security/\n   203\u2192\n   204\u2192---\n   205\u2192\n   206\u2192*(END OF ADR)*\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"

"     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192# Architecture Decision Record 003  \n     3\u2192**Pluggable Cryptography Strategy**\n     4\u2192\n     5\u2192| Status | Proposed |\n     6\u2192| ------ | -------- |\n     7\u2192| Date   | 2024-05-05 |\n     8\u2192| Target release | `v0.8.0` (`CanvasChain Symphony`) |\n     9\u2192| Supersedes | \u2014 |\n    10\u2192| Related ADRs | ADR-001 Modular Micro-services, ADR-002 Event Bus |\n    11\u2192\n    12\u2192---\n    13\u2192\n    14\u2192## 1. Context\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192CanvasChain Symphony aims to be the de-facto playground for experimental digital art on the blockchain.  \n    17\u2192Consequently, we must:\n    18\u2192\n    19\u21921. Support *multiple* signature schemes\u2014`Ed25519` for mainstream wallets, `BLS12-381` for aggregated votes, and one or more post-quantum candidates (e.g. `Dilithium`, `Falcon`) for future-proofing.\n    20\u21922. Allow *runtime* selection of a scheme for each micro-service (e.g. the **governance** service needs BLS while **composition** might stick with Ed25519 for speed).\n    21\u21923. Offer *hot-swap* capabilities so research collectives can ship cryptographic experiments without forking or recompiling the **entire** chain.\n    22\u21924. Maintain *deterministic* behavior across WASM smart-contracts and native nodes so that consensus is never broken.\n    23\u21925. Remain *auditable* and *testable*\u2014adding new crypto must not impair formal verification or fuzzing pipelines.\n    24\u2192\n    25\u2192## 2. Decision\n    26\u2192\n    27\u2192We will implement a **Strategy Pattern** that surfaces an `CryptoSuite` trait across all micro-services.  \n    28\u2192A concrete suite is loaded **at startup** according to configuration (environment variable, CLI flag, or chain parameter) and injected via dependency-injection (gRPC metadata and event bus headers propagate the chosen suite).\n    29\u2192\n    30\u2192Key points:\n    31\u2192\n    32\u2192* The `CryptoSuite` trait is **no-std** compatible so that the same code compiles to WASM.\n    33\u2192* Each suite resides in its own crate (`canvas_crypto_ed25519`, `canvas_crypto_bls`, `canvas_crypto_dilithium`, \u2026) behind a *cargo feature*.\n    34\u2192* We provide a *registry* that maps the on-chain enum discriminator (`CryptoAlgoId`) to a boxed trait object.\n    35\u2192* Critical operations (sign, verify, aggregate, random_seed) are **generic** over the trait, avoiding `dyn` in hot paths.\n    36\u2192* The consensus engine restricts the active set of suites to those that produce deterministic results for VRF.  \n    37\u2192  A governance proposal can *enable* or *disable* a suite network-wide.\n    38\u2192\n    39\u2192### High-level module layout\n    40\u2192\n    41\u2192```\n    42\u2192canvaschain/\n    43\u2192 \u251c\u2500 crates/\n    44\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 crypto_api/       # defines trait + registry\n    45\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 crypto_ed25519/\n    46\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 crypto_bls/\n    47\u2192 \u2502   \u2514\u2500 crypto_dilithium/\n    48\u2192 \u2514\u2500 services/\n    49\u2192     \u251c\u2500 governance/\n    50\u2192     \u251c\u2500 composition/\n    51\u2192     \u2514\u2500 \u2026\n    52\u2192```\n    53\u2192\n    54\u2192### Rust Interface (simplified)\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192```rust\n    57\u2192// crypto_api/src/lib.rs\n    58\u2192#![no_std]\n    59\u2192\n    60\u2192use alloc::boxed::Box;\n    61\u2192use core::fmt::Debug;\n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192pub type Result<T> = core::result::Result<T, CryptoError>;\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192#[derive(Debug)]\n    66\u2192pub enum CryptoError {\n    67\u2192    InvalidKey,\n    68\u2192    InvalidSignature,\n    69\u2192    VerificationFailed,\n    70\u2192    UnsupportedAlgo,\n    71\u2192}\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192pub trait CryptoSuite: Send + Sync + Debug + 'static {\n    74\u2192    const ID: CryptoAlgoId;\n    75\u2192\n    76\u2192    fn generate_keypair(&self, rng: &mut dyn RngCore) -> Result<(PublicKey, PrivateKey)>;\n    77\u2192    fn sign(&self, privkey: &PrivateKey, msg: &[u8]) -> Result<Signature>;\n    78\u2192    fn verify(&self, pubkey: &PublicKey, msg: &[u8], sig: &Signature) -> Result<()>;\n    79\u2192\n    80\u2192    // Optional for schemes that support it\n    81\u2192    fn aggregate(&self, sigs: &[Signature]) -> Result<Signature> {\n    82\u2192        Err(CryptoError::UnsupportedAlgo)\n    83\u2192    }\n    84\u2192}\n    85\u2192\n    86\u2192pub enum CryptoAlgoId {\n    87\u2192    Ed25519,\n    88\u2192    Bls12381,\n    89\u2192    Dilithium5,\n    90\u2192    // \u2026\n    91\u2192}\n    92\u2192\n    93\u2192pub struct SuiteRegistry {\n    94\u2192    inner: spin::RwLock<hashbrown::HashMap<CryptoAlgoId, Box<dyn CryptoSuite>>>,\n    95\u2192}\n    96\u2192\n    97\u2192impl SuiteRegistry {\n    98\u2192    pub const fn new() -> Self { /* \u2026 */ }\n    99\u2192    pub fn register(&self, suite: Box<dyn CryptoSuite>) { /* \u2026 */ }\n   100\u2192    pub fn get(&self, id: CryptoAlgoId) -> Result<&dyn CryptoSuite> { /* \u2026 */ }\n   101\u2192}\n   102\u2192```\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192## 3. Consequences\n   105\u2192\n   106\u2192### Positive\n   107\u2192\n   108\u2192* **Extensibility**: New crypto only requires a new crate implementing `CryptoSuite` and an entry in the registry.\n   109\u2192* **Selective compilation**: Production nodes can compile with `--no-default-features --features \"ed25519 bls\"` to minimize the binary\u2019s attack surface.\n   110\u2192* **WASM parity**: Smart-contracts rely on the same trait, guaranteeing deterministic crypto across FFI boundaries.\n   111\u2192* **Governance control**: The registry honors an on-chain allow-list, so malicious or broken suites can be disabled without a hard-fork.\n   112\u2192\n   113\u2192### Negative / Trade-offs\n   114\u2192\n   115\u2192* **Runtime dispatch** adds minimal overhead (~2\u20135 ns) when comparing trait object lookup vs. monomorphized code.\n   116\u2192* **Larger codebase**: Each algorithm introduces external dependencies (`blst`, `pqcrypto`). Extra scrutiny is required for audits.\n   117\u2192* **Complex migration** if the active suite for validators changes (requires key rotation mechanics).\n   118\u2192\n   119\u2192## 4. Alternatives considered\n   120\u2192\n   121\u21921. **Compile-time feature gating only**  \n   122\u2192   Reject because it forbids late activation of new algorithms by governance.\n   123\u21922. **Dynamic linking to system crypto libraries**  \n   124\u2192   Reject due to WASM determinism concerns and platform-specific quirks.\n   125\u21923. **One-size-fits-all (ED25519 only)**  \n   126\u2192   Reject; stifles experimentation and future-proofing against quantum attacks.\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192## 5. Implementation plan\n   129\u2192\n   130\u21921. Land `crypto_api` crate with trait, error types, and `SuiteRegistry`.  \n   131\u21922. Port existing ED25519 utilities to `canvas_crypto_ed25519`; register by default.  \n   132\u21923. Integrate `blst` and expose `canvas_crypto_bls`.  \n   133\u21924. Scaffold a proof-of-concept `canvas_crypto_dilithium` (behind `experimental` feature).  \n   134\u21925. Update all micro-services to inject `SuiteRegistry` from their service bootstrap.  \n   135\u21926. Add CLI flag `--crypto-suite=[ed25519|bls|dilithium]` for node operators.  \n   136\u21927. Extend governance pallet to manage the on-chain allow-list.  \n   137\u21928. Write cross-suite property tests and differential fuzzers (via `cargo-fuzz`).  \n   138\u21929. Perform third-party audit before enabling `dilithium` on mainnet.\n   139\u2192\n   140\u2192## 6. Security considerations\n   141\u2192\n   142\u2192* Using *multiple* cryptographic primitives increases the surface area for supply-chain attacks. Each suite is audited independently.\n   143\u2192* Each suite\u2019s implementation must meet **constant-time** guarantees.  \n   144\u2192  CI integrates `criterion-ct` to detect data-dependent timing.\n   145\u2192* The registry denies loading suites compiled with *unsafe optimizations* (e.g., `-C target-cpu=native`) unless explicitly whitelisted by validators.\n   146\u2192* Key-material memory is zeroized via `zeroize` crate to mitigate side-channel leaks.\n   147\u2192\n   148\u2192## 7. Reference implementation\n   149\u2192\n   150\u2192Refer to `examples/demo_pluggable_crypto.rs` for a runnable showcase.  \n   151\u2192The demo spins up a mock governance vote that swaps from Ed25519 to BLS mid-session and re-verifies historical signatures.\n   152\u2192\n   153\u2192```\n   154\u2192cargo run --example demo_pluggable_crypto --features \"ed25519 bls\"\n   155\u2192```\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192---\n   158\u2192\n   159\u2192*Prepared by*: `@rust_blockchain_nft_expert`  \n   160\u2192*Reviewed by*: `core-team, cryptography-guild`  \n   161\u2192*Last updated*: 2024-05-05\n   162\u2192```\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. During the same epoch, these staking positions\n    66\u2192also determine governance voting power.\n    67\u2192\n    68\u2192---\n    69\u2192\n    70\u2192## 3. Proposal Lifecycle\n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192```\n    73\u2192Draft \u2192 Review \u2192 Voting \u2192 Enactment (\u21bb or \u26d4)\n    74\u2192```\n    75\u2192\n    76\u2192Phase        | Duration | Key Actors                    | Abort \u20ac\n    77\u2192-------------|----------|------------------------------|--------\n    78\u2192Draft        | \u221e        | Author                       | Free\n    79\u2192Review       | 48 h     | Council (optional)           | \u00b10.1 C\n    80\u2192Voting       | 72 h     | Token-Holders & Delegates    | Bond\n    81\u2192Enactment    | 24 h     | Runtime Scheduler + VRF      | \u2013\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192*Abort fee is burned to discourage spam.*\n    84\u2192\n    85\u2192### 3.1 State Machine\n    86\u2192\n    87\u2192The following Rust enum matches the state machine stored on-chain:\n    88\u2192\n    89\u2192```rust\n    90\u2192/// Governance proposal lifecycle.\n    91\u2192#[derive(scale::Encode, scale::Decode, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]\n    92\u2192pub enum ProposalStage {\n    93\u2192    Draft,\n    94\u2192    Review { started_at: BlockNumber },\n    95\u2192    Voting { ends_at: BlockNumber },\n    96\u2192    Enactment { scheduled_for: BlockNumber },\n    97\u2192    Rejected,\n    98\u2192    Executed,\n    99\u2192}\n   100\u2192```\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192---\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192## 4. Voting & Delegation Model\n   105\u2192\n   106\u21921 `CNOTE` staked = **1 voting unit**.  \n   107\u2192Voters may **delegate** to any on-chain account (wallet, DAO\n   108\u2192multisig, or artist profile). Delegations are *revocable* at any\n   109\u2192time before the snapshot block.\n   110\u2192\n   111\u2192### 4.1 Conviction Escalation\n   112\u2192\n   113\u2192Inspired by Polkadot\u2019s conviction-voting, longer lockups multiply\n   114\u2192weight:\n   115\u2192\n   116\u2192Lockup (blocks) | Multiplier\n   117\u2192---------------|-----------\n   118\u21920              | \u00d71\n   119\u219280 k (\u22481 week) | \u00d72\n   120\u2192320 k          | \u00d73\n   121\u21921 280 k        | \u00d74\n   122\u2192\n   123\u2192---\n   124\u2192\n   125\u2192## 5.           );\n   202\u2192\n   203\u2192            let author = self.env().caller();\n   204\u2192            let id = self.next_id;\n   205\u2192            self.next_id += 1;\n   206\u2192\n   207\u2192            let proposal = Proposal {\n   208\u2192                author,\n   209\u2192                ipfs_hash,\n   210\u2192                stage: ProposalStage::Draft,\n   211\u2192                aye: 0,\n   212\u2192                nay: 0,\n   213\u2192                abstain: 0,\n   214\u2192                vetoed: false,\n   215\u2192            };\n   216\u2192\n   217\u2192            self.proposals.insert(id, &proposal);\n   218\u2192            self.env().emit_event(NewProposal { id, author });\n   219\u2192            id\n   220\u2192        }\n   221\u2192\n   222\u2192        /// Cast a vote with conviction weight.\n   223\u2192        #[ink(message)]\n   224\u2192        pub fn vote(\n   225\u2192            &mut self,\n   226\u2192            id: ProposalId,\n 245\u2192\n   246\u2192            self.proposals.insert(id, &p);\n   247\u2192            self.env().emit_event(VoteCast {\n   248\u2192                id,\n   249\u2192                voter: self.env().caller(),\n   250\u2192                kind,\n   251\u2192                weight,\n   252\u2192            });\n   253\u2192            Ok(())\n   254\u2192        }\n   255\u2192\n   256\u2192        // Additional methods: advance_stage, veto, execute, etc.\n   257\u2192    }\n   258\u2192\n   259\u2192    /// EVENTS -----------------------------------------------------\n   260\u2192    #[ink(event)]\n   261\u2192    pub struct NewProposal {\n   262\u2192        #[ink(topic)]\n   263\u2192        id: ProposalId,\n   264\u2192        #[ink(topic)]\n   265\u2192 ERRORS -----------------------------------------------------\n   279\u2192    #[derive(Debug, Encode, Decode)]\n   280\u2192    #[cfg_attr(feature = \"std\", derive(scale_info::TypeInfo))]\n   281\u2192    pub enum GovernanceError {\n   282\u2192        ProposalMissing,\n   283\u2192        NotInVoting,\n   284\u2192        Unauthorized,\n   285\u2192    }\n   286\u2192\n   287\u2192    fn ensure(cond: bool, err: GovernanceError) -> Result<(), GovernanceError> {\n   288\u2192        if cond {\n   289\u2192            Ok(())\n   290\u2192        } else {\n   291\u2192
